For instance, the English sentence "So, you know, here I am now" was translated to "Na und da sitze ich nun" in German, where the adverbial clause ("so" / "na und") is followed by the subject ("you" / "ich") and then the verb ("know" / "sitze"). I arrived at this translation by analyzing the sentence structure of the English source and comparing it to the German examples provided. In English, the sentence is constructed using the modal verb "would" followed by the base form of the verb "have", which expresses past counterfactual conditionality. The main clause "This be fine" uses the copular verb "be" and the subject "this" along with the adjective "fine". In German, this sentence structure can be translated using the Konjunktiv II form of the verb "sein", which in this case is "wäre", followed by "in Ordnung", the German equivalent of "fine". The subject "dies" (this) remains in its base form.
